# 1. Executive Verdict

## 1.1 One-Sentence Verdict  

The DATP paper is strong conference-level and journal‑near, but it still lacks the experimental breadth, comparative baselines, temporal analysis, and privacy/robustness treatment expected for an Elsevier security journal. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/54884680/7ec30c4e-be1a-4fa0-b512-ec2a89e1b24a/DATP-2.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEYNG77JJY&Signature=SKSXxKjHlouVeY4i09ca4sRbLGk%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEGsaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJHMEUCIQDFD8U6n20wgYy1lIWIUpx72WUp1%2BGzNhldJ8KR7WlnWAIgVSnYqCDWyvA0z%2B%2BMGA7xMDyMknLgcrZJGBYD8Z07NFgq8wQINBABGgw2OTk3NTMzMDk3MDUiDIgD5Me8%2FBcD9UTOoCrQBB9K5xQ66rGx9FVJ367oGZzxh%2ByEF3N5yU4FUrqbWcLkeilDY3MKsEdF5p7fNvuEpQ0Eyxf%2BWvBF6VifAtqi%2B8HcY%2Fwof0Pzg8sCvoHwwBpJj3ftj2h2wLqSu79JWq%2BnC1e4u0sZm2OaBiFeufhflrrAqTWMVuVcx4cuohoW4LLY5S1YhWmgywpZXNKmujmhbAaEDIHVSRhp94gtFkLUHwi5bDdSnBejGKJKBe7M%2BK9xueEfWTpGaLA9aFAioS2rvc%2BJb0g5ZFwW2lkOvJ7A88lCGT7%2BpaRz2NU7MlAu6BYezDgEjd%2F34CwqwJTCJFWOg1xTXHp2ByTWLYTWWBCf9ckOcLB2NtQz6Y3xSL3pEQ9IxMMskGNUpDQgIT8Cu4%2BTTTtcZ6CjqLdLMi5SDklTnAeYx2ueJpGOLy2RSXvSqg%2Fp0dE%2BuDJrnGcYGNy%2B42Ur6n%2BcPoWkNo2ZfYrTaMTesRPqxqBklXDqh1MJNLRGwFRtm6TzA3N6WSU97oKFIULgKVERss%2B7f%2BrIjbf6ns3vuOfopD4uGVi77CisoDINPNgvlJL3jPNHUvTpNpsGs%2F9mcGCErrI6ppw2zvEqRoE5pH8yn7wkiWDK5Uy83w58ze6hjYjBUDGQBf9M68SUCu%2BwYjzGRZf1U1W0CZOFR4mJCldbYj79NB2IsnvM%2BCg9%2B9u%2FahEs%2FXH67Q2lPtNgIYLqO6BP3w4XE9Qtn4MUd2Zr0Ke2udWY2R5BfSDLWxqwW9n3UbQ4hXcSCGi68cYLp53ByhArGWvkVcI0GmqICP8ZjVYwp4vG0AY6mAHjy%2FNerQHKG%2F7RMQtjydR%2Bq6jb3N9S44wIeSfIs7VhVQ3nHYzSJJkoAuGHCSRe4wjRREgZV5JEQYr94XlTMcit6HLxOBRGWPn9TxzfHGy6uwsoQ1sUF5ud6i2bY%2B3M2xwY0xNcVvpwwCgiRxQpgJuFYfB3umIN3%2Fd3lsocKZdTQgND0mlvHvCAocBswrSMUvnkl2V042gobQ%3D%3D&Expires=1779536244)

## 1.2 Journal Extension Feasibility  

A strong journal extension is clearly feasible: the encoder, FL pipeline, score artifacts, and replication package are solid, the research question is sharply scoped (threshold scope only), and there is clear room for additional datasets, threshold variants, comparisons, and analyses without changing DATP’s identity. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/54884680/d7bca94c-149b-43b0-923a-7f635d7ab3f7/State_of_the_Art.md?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEYNG77JJY&Signature=%2BZWkfVFuHRTcIbiief1CY6bsKa0%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEGsaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJHMEUCIQDFD8U6n20wgYy1lIWIUpx72WUp1%2BGzNhldJ8KR7WlnWAIgVSnYqCDWyvA0z%2B%2BMGA7xMDyMknLgcrZJGBYD8Z07NFgq8wQINBABGgw2OTk3NTMzMDk3MDUiDIgD5Me8%2FBcD9UTOoCrQBB9K5xQ66rGx9FVJ367oGZzxh%2ByEF3N5yU4FUrqbWcLkeilDY3MKsEdF5p7fNvuEpQ0Eyxf%2BWvBF6VifAtqi%2B8HcY%2Fwof0Pzg8sCvoHwwBpJj3ftj2h2wLqSu79JWq%2BnC1e4u0sZm2OaBiFeufhflrrAqTWMVuVcx4cuohoW4LLY5S1YhWmgywpZXNKmujmhbAaEDIHVSRhp94gtFkLUHwi5bDdSnBejGKJKBe7M%2BK9xueEfWTpGaLA9aFAioS2rvc%2BJb0g5ZFwW2lkOvJ7A88lCGT7%2BpaRz2NU7MlAu6BYezDgEjd%2F34CwqwJTCJFWOg1xTXHp2ByTWLYTWWBCf9ckOcLB2NtQz6Y3xSL3pEQ9IxMMskGNUpDQgIT8Cu4%2BTTTtcZ6CjqLdLMi5SDklTnAeYx2ueJpGOLy2RSXvSqg%2Fp0dE%2BuDJrnGcYGNy%2B42Ur6n%2BcPoWkNo2ZfYrTaMTesRPqxqBklXDqh1MJNLRGwFRtm6TzA3N6WSU97oKFIULgKVERss%2B7f%2BrIjbf6ns3vuOfopD4uGVi77CisoDINPNgvlJL3jPNHUvTpNpsGs%2F9mcGCErrI6ppw2zvEqRoE5pH8yn7wkiWDK5Uy83w58ze6hjYjBUDGQBf9M68SUCu%2BwYjzGRZf1U1W0CZOFR4mJCldbYj79NB2IsnvM%2BCg9%2B9u%2FahEs%2FXH67Q2lPtNgIYLqO6BP3w4XE9Qtn4MUd2Zr0Ke2udWY2R5BfSDLWxqwW9n3UbQ4hXcSCGi68cYLp53ByhArGWvkVcI0GmqICP8ZjVYwp4vG0AY6mAHjy%2FNerQHKG%2F7RMQtjydR%2Bq6jb3N9S44wIeSfIs7VhVQ3nHYzSJJkoAuGHCSRe4wjRREgZV5JEQYr94XlTMcit6HLxOBRGWPn9TxzfHGy6uwsoQ1sUF5ud6i2bY%2B3M2xwY0xNcVvpwwCgiRxQpgJuFYfB3umIN3%2Fd3lsocKZdTQgND0mlvHvCAocBswrSMUvnkl2V042gobQ%3D%3D&Expires=1779536244)

## 1.3 Most Important Upgrade  

The single most important upgrade is: **add a second, well-justified IoT(-like) traffic dataset with a meaningful client notion and run the full B1–B2–B4 ladder plus deeper per-client analyses**, to show that DATP’s threshold‑personalization story is not an N‑BaIoT one‑off. [frontiersin](https://www.frontiersin.org/journals/big-data/articles/10.3389/fdata.2025.1526480/full)

## 1.4 Main Danger  

The main danger is expanding into model‑personalization, robust aggregation, or generic FL‑IDS algorithm benchmarking to “compete” with FedBN, Per‑FedAvg, FedMSE, Tab‑Transformer IDS, etc., thereby losing the threshold‑calibration identity and creating an over‑broad, under‑deep journal paper. [arxiv](https://arxiv.org/html/2410.09284v1)

***

# 2. Current Paper Reconstruction

| Item | Extracted From Paper | Reviewer Interpretation |
|---|---|---|
| Core contribution | Threshold scope is isolated as the only experimental variable: one FedAvg AE is trained per seed and reused across four threshold policies (B1 shared, B2 per‑client, B3 family mean, B4 cluster mean) on N‑BaIoT and CICIoT2023, with CV(FPR) as the primary metric. | Exploratory evidence | Cluster‑mean B4 with K=3 on N‑BaIoT benign summaries [µ, σ, skew, p95] recovers ≈42–59% of B2’s CV(FPR) reduction; Dirichlet regime C with K=20 synthetic clients sweeps α∈{0.1,…,IID} and shows the B1–B2 gap grows as heterogeneity increases and flips sign under IID. | Transferable FL methods | FedBN, Per‑FedAvg, LG‑FedAvg as model‑personalization for feature‑shift/label‑skew; FedProx, FedAvgM, adaptive optimizers; MSEAvg weighting for heterogeneity (P029); clustered FL and split/partial sharing; reconstruction‑style self‑supervised FL (masked AEs). # 4. Weakness Matrix

(Only key weaknesses listed; IDs W01–W15 are stable.)

| ID | Weakness | Severity | Evidence From Paper | Why Reviewer Cares | Fix Type | New Experiment Needed | Effort | Scope Drift Risk |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| W01 | Single real device‑level dataset (N‑BaIoT K=9) plus one pseudo‑client dataset (CICIoT2023 files); no second physical‑client IoT dataset. | Critical | Regimes A–C all based on N‑BaIoT; Regime B uses CICIoT2023 file‑level pseudo‑clients. apply B1/B2/B4 with q=0.95 and quantile sweep; report CV(FPR), FPR/TPR trade‑off, worst BA, P10 Macro‑F1, and JS divergence between clients. | New dataset (Edge‑IIoTset or UNSW‑NB15 as “adjacent”) | Same threshold policies (B1–B4) plus chosen external threshold baseline (see W03) | Same metrics as Regime A, plus calibration coverage and maybe AUC | Main | Demonstrates that per‑client calibration and cluster‑mean grouping generalize beyond N‑BaIoT; | W02 | Replace/augment Regime B with a more realistic CICIoT2023 client partition: group by IoT device, attack scenario, or time slice rather than random MERGED_CSV files, and redo the B1–B2–B4 comparison. | CICIoT2023 original paper emphasizes large‑scale multi‑device, multi‑attack scenarios with device and source IDs. | W03 | Implement one federated summary‑statistics‑based global threshold as an additional *threshold* baseline on top of your stored AE scores (e.g., Laridi et al.’s method that aggregates mean/variance/skew/kurtosis across clients and searches thresholds in the overlap region). | Laridi et al. (2024) propose a federated threshold using summary statistics from both normal and anomalous data, outperforming simple global and local methods under non‑IID; they specifically contrast local vs federated thresholds.  [arxiv](https://arxiv.org/html/2410.09284v1) | On the existing score artifacts, compute local summary statistics; aggregate them to approximate Laridi’s Fed Threshold (or a simplified variant that uses global statistics and F1‑based selection on a held‑out validation subset), and compare its CV(FPR), F1, and robustness with B1/B2/B4. | Existing N‑BaIoT, CICIoT2023, new dataset from W01 | New baseline family: summary‑statistics global threshold | CV(FPR), F1, CV(TPR), P10 Macro‑F1, robustness to non‑IID severity band | Main | Directly addresses the most relevant recent threshold work; strengthens novelty claim: DATP studies *device‑aware* vs *global* thresholding under an identical AE, not just local vs global. |

| W09 | Expand threshold variant analysis: (i) formal q‑sweep (0.90, 0.95, 0.99) for B1/B2/B4 reported systematically, (ii) add one local‑global shrinkage threshold τk = λτk,p95 + (1−λ)τglobal with λ depending on calibration size, and (iii) evaluate whether shrinkage mitigates P10 Macro‑F1 degradation while preserving CV(FPR) reduction. | Local vs global threshold trade‑offs and calibration‑size issues are discussed in federated thresholding work and in IoT AD literature.  [arxiv](https://arxiv.org/html/2410.09284v1) | Using stored scores, recompute thresholds: B1/B2/B4 at q∈{0.90,0.95,0.99}; implement shrinkage threshold with λ∈{0.5,0.75,1} or a simple size‑dependent λ; report CV(FPR), CV(TPR), P10 Macro‑F1; identify a recommended operating point. | Existing datasets | Same policies + shrinkage | Same metrics | Main | Shows that the chosen q=0.95 is not arbitrary and that you have explored simple, deployable variants to manage the fairness vs detection trade‑off. |
| W10 | Correlate per‑client benign divergence (e.g., JS, Wasserstein) or differences in p95 with observed FPR dispersion and DATP benefit (B1–B2 and B1–B4 ∆). | SoA emphasizes heterogeneity type and magnitude; CICIoT2023 Regime B already uses JS divergence. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/54884680/d7bca94c-149b-43b0-923a-7f635d7ab3f7/State_of_the_Art.md?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEYNG77JJY&Signature=%2BZWkfVFuHRTcIbiief1CY6bsKa0%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEGsaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJHMEUCIQDFD8U6n20wgYy1lIWIUpx72WUp1%2BGzNhldJ8KR7WlnWAIgVSnYqCDWyvA0z%2B%2BMGA7xMDyMknLgcrZJGBYD8Z07NFgq8wQINBABGgw2OTk3NTMzMDk3MDUiDIgD5Me8%2FBcD9UTOoCrQBB9K5xQ66rGx9FVJ367oGZzxh%2ByEF3N5yU4FUrqbWcLkeilDY3MKsEdF5p7fNvuEpQ0Eyxf%2BWvBF6VifAtqi%2B8HcY%2Fwof0Pzg8sCvoHwwBpJj3ftj2h2wLqSu79JWq%2BnC1e4u0sZm2OaBiFeufhflrrAqTWMVuVcx4cuohoW4LLY5S1YhWmgywpZXNKmujmhbAaEDIHVSRhp94gtFkLUHwi5bDdSnBejGKJKBe7M%2BK9xueEfWTpGaLA9aFAioS2rvc%2BJb0g5ZFwW2lkOvJ7A88lCGT7%2BpaRz2NU7MlAu6BYezDgEjd%2F34CwqwJTCJFWOg1xTXHp2ByTWLYTWWBCf9ckOcLB2NtQz6Y3xSL3pEQ9IxMMskGNUpDQgIT8Cu4%2BTTTtcZ6CjqLdLMi5SDklTnAeYx2ueJpGOLy2RSXvSqg%2Fp0dE%2BuDJrnGcYGNy%2B42Ur6n%2BcPoWkNo2ZfYrTaMTesRPqxqBklXDqh1MJNLRGwFRtm6TzA3N6WSU97oKFIULgKVERss%2B7f%2BrIjbf6ns3vuOfopD4uGVi77CisoDINPNgvlJL3jPNHUvTpNpsGs%2F9mcGCErrI6ppw2zvEqRoE5pH8yn7wkiWDK5Uy83w58ze6hjYjBUDGQBf9M68SUCu%2BwYjzGRZf1U1W0CZOFR4mJCldbYj79NB2IsnvM%2BCg9%2B9u%2FahEs%2FXH67Q2lPtNgIYLqO6BP3w4XE9Qtn4MUd2Zr0Ke2udWY2R5BfSDLWxqwW9n3UbQ4hXcSCGi68cYLp53ByhArGWvkVcI0GmqICP8ZjVYwp4vG0AY6mAHjy%2FNerQHKG%2F7RMQtjydR%2Bq6jb3N9S44wIeSfIs7VhVQ3nHYzSJJkoAuGHCSRe4wjRREgZV5JEQYr94XlTMcit6HLxOBRGWPn9TxzfHGy6uwsoQ1sUF5ud6i2bY%2B3M2xwY0xNcVvpwwCgiRxQpgJuFYfB3umIN3%2Fd3lsocKZdTQgND0mlvHvCAocBswrSMUvnkl2V042gobQ%3D%3D&Expires=1779536244) | No natural physical device notion. | Limited. | Possible but clients would be artificial. | Weak: device‑aware personalization becomes contrived. | Moderate. | Adds little to DATP’s unique angle; may be seen as “tick‑box” dataset. |
| IoT‑23 | Maybe add (if a clean device/host split can be designed and documentation confirms suitability) | Public IoT malware dataset with real infected devices; promising candidate but details not fully examined here (“Not found in available sources” beyond general knowledge). | Likely yes (devices and attacks), but **details not found in available sources in this session**. | Likely yes. | Likely good, pending data exploration. | Potentially excellent second IoT dataset if client mapping is clear. | Unknown here; assume medium. | Incomplete information; risk of under‑analyzed preprocessing and mispartitioning. |
| Edge‑IIoTset | Add as primary *new* dataset, if client mapping is tractable | Widely used IIoT / edge dataset; recent FL‑IDS work uses it to evaluate CNN–BiLSTM‑based IDS and FL frameworks.  [frontiersin](https://www.frontiersin.org/journals/big-data/articles/10.3389/fdata.2025.1526480/full) | Yes in principle (edge devices / PLCs / nodes), but exact mapping requires dataset study (not fully documented here). | Likely yes (industrial traffic over time). | Should support benign calibration and attack test partitions. | Strong: extends DATP story to industrial IoT / edge with more devices and different traffic characteristics. | Likely moderate–high. | Preprocessing and client definition effort; if mapping is weak, reviewers may question “device‑aware” label. |

**Recommendation:**  

- **Add** exactly **one new “true IoT/IIoT” dataset** in the *must‑do* package: Edge‑IIoTset (or ToN‑IoT if, after local inspection, Edge‑IIoTset proves too awkward), with a clearly defined device/host client notion. - Treat UNSW‑NB15, IoT‑23, Bot‑IoT as **optional or future work** to avoid scope drift.

# 8. Threshold Variant Matrix

(Existing B1–B4 kept; below are *new* variants to consider.)

| Variant | Definition | Why It Matters | Mandatory? | Risk | Main or Supplement |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| Quantile sweep | Evaluate B1/B2/B4 at q∈{0.90,0.95,0.99} systematically, not just a brief sensitivity check.  [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/54884680/7ec30c4e-be1a-4fa0-b512-ec2a89e1b24a/DATP-2.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEYNG77JJY&Signature=SKSXxKjHlouVeY4i09ca4sRbLGk%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEGsaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJHMEUCIQDFD8U6n20wgYy1lIWIUpx72WUp1%2BGzNhldJ8KR7WlnWAIgVSnYqCDWyvA0z%2B%2BMGA7xMDyMknLgcrZJGBYD8Z07NFgq8wQINBABGgw2OTk3NTMzMDk3MDUiDIgD5Me8%2FBcD9UTOoCrQBB9K5xQ66rGx9FVJ367oGZzxh%2ByEF3N5yU4FUrqbWcLkeilDY3MKsEdF5p7fNvuEpQ0Eyxf%2BWvBF6VifAtqi%2B8HcY%2Fwof0Pzg8sCvoHwwBpJj3ftj2h2wLqSu79JWq%2BnC1e4u0sZm2OaBiFeufhflrrAqTWMVuVcx4cuohoW4LLY5S1YhWmgywpZXNKmujmhbAaEDIHVSRhp94gtFkLUHwi5bDdSnBejGKJKBe7M%2BK9xueEfWTpGaLA9aFAioS2rvc%2BJb0g5ZFwW2lkOvJ7A88lCGT7%2BpaRz2NU7MlAu6BYezDgEjd%2F34CwqwJTCJFWOg1xTXHp2ByTWLYTWWBCf9ckOcLB2NtQz6Y3xSL3pEQ9IxMMskGNUpDQgIT8Cu4%2BTTTtcZ6CjqLdLMi5SDklTnAeYx2ueJpGOLy2RSXvSqg%2Fp0dE%2BuDJrnGcYGNy%2B42Ur6n%2BcPoWkNo2ZfYrTaMTesRPqxqBklXDqh1MJNLRGwFRtm6TzA3N6WSU97oKFIULgKVERss%2B7f%2BrIjbf6ns3vuOfopD4uGVi77CisoDINPNgvlJL3jPNHUvTpNpsGs%2F9mcGCErrI6ppw2zvEqRoE5pH8yn7wkiWDK5Uy83w58ze6hjYjBUDGQBf9M68SUCu%2BwYjzGRZf1U1W0CZOFR4mJCldbYj79NB2IsnvM%2BCg9%2B9u%2FahEs%2FXH67Q2lPtNgIYLqO6BP3w4XE9Qtn4MUd2Zr0Ke2udWY2R5BfSDLWxqwW9n3UbQ4hXcSCGi68cYLp53ByhArGWvkVcI0GmqICP8ZjVYwp4vG0AY6mAHjy%2FNerQHKG%2F7RMQtjydR%2Bq6jb3N9S44wIeSfIs7VhVQ3nHYzSJJkoAuGHCSRe4wjRREgZV5JEQYr94XlTMcit6HLxOBRGWPn9TxzfHGy6uwsoQ1sUF5ud6i2bY%2B3M2xwY0xNcVvpwwCgiRxQpgJuFYfB3umIN3%2Fd3lsocKZdTQgND0mlvHvCAocBswrSMUvnkl2V042gobQ%3D%3D&Expires=1779536244) | Shows robustness of dispersion and P10 Macro‑F1 behavior to threshold level; may reveal safer operating points (e.g., slightly lower q to reduce missed attacks). | Yes | Low – purely analytical. | Main (short subsection). |
| Local‑global shrinkage | For client k: τk(λ)=λτk,p95 + (1−λ)τglobal, with λ constant or a function of calibration sample size. | Interpolates between full personalization and global sharing; can mitigate overfitting on small calibration sets and smooth extreme thresholds. | Yes (one or two λ values) | Low–Medium – must avoid over‑fitting λ. | Main (as an additional threshold policy B2.5). |
| Summary‑stats global threshold | Federated threshold based on aggregated summary statistics and overlap‑region search (simplified Laridi method).  [arxiv](https://arxiv.org/html/2410.09284v1) | Acts as a strong global competitor that explicitly uses anomalies and validation F1 to set thresholds; tests whether DATP is still needed. | Yes | Low – but must be described as approximation if not replicated exactly. | Main (as separate baseline). |
| Calibration‑size‑aware fallback | Clients with n<nmin use shrinkage or global threshold instead of pure local percentile; report behavior as function of nmin. | Real deployments often have scarce benign data; this variant assesses DATP’s practicality under calibration starvation. | Recommended | Low | Supplement (or integrated into local‑global shrinkage analysis). |
| Robust cluster median | Replace cluster mean in B4 with cluster‑wise median of τk,p95; optionally drop small clusters. | Makes B4 less sensitive to outlier clients; may change metadata‑leakage profile slightly. | Optional | Low | Supplement (if time permits). |

**New threshold variants to keep within the “max 4” constraint for the *final package*:**

1. Quantile sweep (B1/B2/B4 at q=0.90, 0.95, 0.99).  
2. Local‑global shrinkage τk(λ).  
3. Summary‑statistics global threshold.  
4. Calibration‑size‑aware fallback (can share implementation with shrinkage).

***

# 9. Temporal Drift and Recalibration Plan

## 9.1 Feasibility  

- N‑BaIoT has chronological traces and is already split with temporal gaps; it supports basic temporal drift experiments by calibrating on earlier benign windows and testing later. - CICIoT2023’s MERGED_CSV files as currently used do **not** preserve within‑file time; temporal drift analysis on this partition is **not feasible** (“Not found in available sources” for an easily usable time index here). - New dataset (Edge‑IIoTset or ToN‑IoT) should be inspected for timestamps; drift analysis is optional there.

## 9.2 Minimum Viable Temporal Experiment  

- **Design:**  
  - Choose N‑BaIoT devices with sufficient duration.  
  - Split benign data into early calibration window \(W_0\) and later windows \(W_1,…,W_T\), ensuring no overlap with attack data.  
  - Calibrate B1, B2, B4 on \(W_0\); test on each \(W_t\) without recalibration.  
- **Measurements:**  
  - For each \(W_t\): per‑client FPR, TPR, Macro‑F1; fleet‑level CV(FPR), CV(TPR); worst BA; P10 Macro‑F1.  
- **Goal:**  
  - Quantify *threshold aging* (how quickly dispersion and detection degrade over time under static calibration).

## 9.3 Strong Temporal Experiment  

- Extend the above by **introducing periodic recalibration**:  
  - Every Δt (e.g., after each window \(W_t\)), refresh τ using benign events in \(W_t\) only (online) or \(W_0…W_t\) (cumulative).  
  - Compare static vs periodic recalibration for B1, B2, and shrinkage variants: how many calibration updates are needed to maintain CV(FPR) and P10 Macro‑F1 within acceptable bands?  
- Optionally, if the new dataset has timestamps, replicate the minimal experiment there to show cross‑dataset consistency.

## 9.4 Metrics  

- CV(FPR) and CV(TPR) over time.  
- Mean FPR and TPR over time.  
- Worst‑client BA and P10 Macro‑F1 over time.  
- Number of calibration updates and benign samples consumed.  
- Simple drift indicators (e.g., change in per‑client benign mean error or JS divergence between calibration and test windows). [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/54884680/d7bca94c-149b-43b0-923a-7f635d7ab3f7/State_of_the_Art.md?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEYNG77JJY&Signature=%2BZWkfVFuHRTcIbiief1CY6bsKa0%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEGsaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJHMEUCIQDFD8U6n20wgYy1lIWIUpx72WUp1%2BGzNhldJ8KR7WlnWAIgVSnYqCDWyvA0z%2B%2BMGA7xMDyMknLgcrZJGBYD8Z07NFgq8wQINBABGgw2OTk3NTMzMDk3MDUiDIgD5Me8%2FBcD9UTOoCrQBB9K5xQ66rGx9FVJ367oGZzxh%2ByEF3N5yU4FUrqbWcLkeilDY3MKsEdF5p7fNvuEpQ0Eyxf%2BWvBF6VifAtqi%2B8HcY%2Fwof0Pzg8sCvoHwwBpJj3ftj2h2wLqSu79JWq%2BnC1e4u0sZm2OaBiFeufhflrrAqTWMVuVcx4cuohoW4LLY5S1YhWmgywpZXNKmujmhbAaEDIHVSRhp94gtFkLUHwi5bDdSnBejGKJKBe7M%2BK9xueEfWTpGaLA9aFAioS2rvc%2BJb0g5ZFwW2lkOvJ7A88lCGT7%2BpaRz2NU7MlAu6BYezDgEjd%2F34CwqwJTCJFWOg1xTXHp2ByTWLYTWWBCf9ckOcLB2NtQz6Y3xSL3pEQ9IxMMskGNUpDQgIT8Cu4%2BTTTtcZ6CjqLdLMi5SDklTnAeYx2ueJpGOLy2RSXvSqg%2Fp0dE%2BuDJrnGcYGNy%2B42Ur6n%2BcPoWkNo2ZfYrTaMTesRPqxqBklXDqh1MJNLRGwFRtm6TzA3N6WSU97oKFIULgKVERss%2B7f%2BrIjbf6ns3vuOfopD4uGVi77CisoDINPNgvlJL3jPNHUvTpNpsGs%2F9mcGCErrI6ppw2zvEqRoE5pH8yn7wkiWDK5Uy83w58ze6hjYjBUDGQBf9M68SUCu%2BwYjzGRZf1U1W0CZOFR4mJCldbYj79NB2IsnvM%2BCg9%2B9u%2FahEs%2FXH67Q2lPtNgIYLqO6BP3w4XE9Qtn4MUd2Zr0Ke2udWY2R5BfSDLWxqwW9n3UbQ4hXcSCGi68cYLp53ByhArGWvkVcI0GmqICP8ZjVYwp4vG0AY6mAHjy%2FNerQHKG%2F7RMQtjydR%2Bq6jb3N9S44wIeSfIs7VhVQ3nHYzSJJkoAuGHCSRe4wjRREgZV5JEQYr94XlTMcit6HLxOBRGWPn9TxzfHGy6uwsoQ1sUF5ud6i2bY%2B3M2xwY0xNcVvpwwCgiRxQpgJuFYfB3umIN3%2Fd3lsocKZdTQgND0mlvHvCAocBswrSMUvnkl2V042gobQ%3D%3D&Expires=1779536244)

## 9.5 Interpretation Rules  

- **Positive outcome:**  
  - CV(FPR) and mean FPR remain relatively stable over time, or are restored by periodic recalibration with modest benign data; P10 Macro‑F1 does not collapse.  
  - Interpretation: DATP thresholds age gracefully and can be maintained with low‑frequency recalibration, supporting real deployments.
- **Negative outcome:**  
  - CV(FPR) or P10 Macro‑F1 degrade rapidly despite recalibration, or require very frequent recalibration with large benign volumes.  
  - Interpretation: per‑client calibration is fragile to drift; DATP should then be framed explicitly as a *static deployment study* and drift mitigation left as future work.
- **Mixed outcome:**  
  - Some devices remain stable, others show rapid drift.  
  - Interpretation: leads to nuanced guidance: per‑client thresholds are beneficial for heavily drifting devices only if recalibration is feasible; otherwise cluster‑mean or global thresholds may be preferable for those device types.

***

To respect the “max 6 deeper analyses” constraint in the final package, the **High** and first two **Medium** items are enough.

# 11. Journal Originality and Conference Extension Plan

## 11.1 What Can Be Reused  

- Conceptual framework: threshold scope isolation, research questions RQ1–RQ3, and the main N‑BaIoT Regime A design. - At least **one new IoT/IIoT dataset** with meaningful clients (Edge‑IIoTset or ToN‑IoT), with full B1–B2–B4 + summary‑stats threshold analysis.

## 11.3 Self-Plagiarism Risk  

- Current DATP text and figures would likely overlap heavily (especially introduction, methodology, N‑BaIoT tables/figures).  
- To avoid self‑plagiarism:  
  - Rewrite introduction and related‑work sections substantially, integrating new literature and framing.  
  - Redraw and expand figures: add new datasets, new threshold variants, temporal plots; reuse only a subset of N‑BaIoT plots.  
  - Replace tables with extended versions that include new baselines/datasets and CIs.  
  - Ensure that the journal paper *cites* the conference version and clearly states which parts are reused and which are new. [sciencedirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/abs/pii/S0306261926006999)

## 11.4 Cover Letter Disclosure (Draft 5–8 Sentences)  

> This manuscript is an extended version of our conference paper “Device‑Aware Threshold Personalization: A Controlled Threshold‑Calibration Study for Non‑IID Federated IoT Anomaly Detection” (DATP), which is currently under consideration/accepted at [conference name]. In DATP, we introduced a threshold‑scope‑only evaluation of per‑client percentile calibration on N‑BaIoT and file‑level CICIoT2023 partitions under a fixed FedAvg autoencoder. In the present journal version, we substantially extend this work along four axes. First, we add a second IoT/IIoT dataset with a realistic client notion and redesign the CICIoT2023 partition, demonstrating when device‑aware thresholds generalize beyond N‑BaIoT and when they do not. Second, we introduce additional thresholding strategies, including a federated summary‑statistics global threshold and local‑global shrinkage, and we analyze their behavior under a non‑IID severity sweep. Third, we incorporate temporal drift and recalibration experiments, calibration‑size sensitivity analyses, and fairness‑oriented operational metrics to move from static evaluation to deployment‑oriented guidance. Fourth, we update the literature review and comparisons to include recent FL‑IDS and federated thresholding works (e.g., FedMSE, Tab‑Transformer FL IDS, summary‑statistics thresholding), clarifying the distinct role of device‑aware threshold personalization. Together, these additions more than double the experimental content and significantly deepen the analysis compared to the conference version.

***

| Rank | Journal | Scope Match | Indexing Status To Verify | Best Framing Angle | Required Upgrades | Desk-Rejection Risk | Recommendation |
|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | Computers & Security (C&S)  [sciencedirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/journal/computers-and-security) | Strong: leading IT security journal; publishes FL‑IDS, IoT security, anomaly detection, and privacy/robustness work. | Verify JCR IF (~5+), Q1 security; Scopus/SCImago confirm Q1.  [askbisht](https://askbisht.com/journals/computers-and-security) | Emphasize **IoT security, IDS, and privacy/fairness of FL thresholds**; focus on threshold‑personalization as improving operational false‑alarm equity under non‑IID. | Must‑do package (new dataset, improved CICIoT2023 partition, new threshold baselines, temporal analysis, deeper analyses, updated related work). | Medium – will desk‑reject if scope is seen as too narrow or incremental vs FL‑IDS works; clear extension narrative and strong new experiments reduce risk. | **High priority**; primary target. |
| 2 | Computer Networks  [schunter](https://www.schunter.org/blog/wp-content/uploads/2018/05/CfP-Journal-Security-for-the-IoT-v14.pdf) | Strong: publishes FL‑based IoT malware detection, IoT security, and network‑level IDS; has hosted FL‑IDS papers (e.g., Rey et al.). | 3 | Journal of Network and Computer Applications (JNCA)  [askbisht](https://askbisht.com/journals/journal-of-network-and-computer-applications) | Strong: focuses on networked systems and applications, including security and IoT; Q1 with significant impact factor. | Verify latest IF (~8.7) and Q1 standing.  [askbisht](https://askbisht.com/journals/journal-of-network-and-computer-applications) | Emphasize **networked IoT applications and FL‑based IDS**, with a slightly stronger systems/deployment angle (fairness, overhead, applicability guidelines). | Same as C&S; fairness and operational analysis are particularly relevant. | Medium – but may be more open to a specialized threshold‑oriented FL‑IDS paper if experiments are rich. | High priority (third choice). |
| 4 | Internet of Things: Engineering Cyber Physical Human Systems  [sciencedirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/journal/internet-of-things) | Good: broad IoT & cyber‑physical scope, including security and AIoT.  [sciencedirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/journal/internet-of-things) | Verify indexing (Scopus, JCR; not all details retrieved).  [scholar9](https://scholar9.com/journal/internet-of-things-elsevier-16602) | Frame as **IoT systems paper** focusing on collaborative anomaly detection and device‑aware thresholding in IoT fleets, with less emphasis on cryptography. | Same core upgrades; may require more system‑level discussion and case‑study style guidance. | Medium–High – IoT is broad; editor may consider work too security‑specific unless framed carefully. | Medium priority. |
| 5 | Future Generation Computer Systems (FGCS)  [sciencedirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/journal/future-generation-computer-systems) | Moderate: focuses on distributed systems, clouds, IoT infrastructures; security is relevant but not central. | Verify indexing (Q1).  [sciencedirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/journal/future-generation-computer-systems) | Emphasize **distributed FL infrastructure, non‑IID heterogeneity, and threshold calibration as a distributed systems problem**. | Might need more emphasis on distributed aspects and possibly performance. | High – risk of scope mismatch unless you extend systems angle. | Low–Medium priority. |
| 6 | Engineering Applications of Artificial Intelligence (EAAI) | Moderate: method‑centric AI journal; could fit if DATP is pitched as an AI/thresholding method widely applicable beyond IoT. | Verify indexing and scope via Guide for Authors (not retrieved here). | Frame as **federated anomaly‑detection method** with thresholding innovations, possibly downplaying IoT specificity. | Would require broader non‑IoT datasets and more methodological positioning; risks scope drift. | High – paper may be seen as too application‑specific. | Low priority (not recommended for primary submission). |
| 7 | Computer Standards & Interfaces  [sciencedirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/journal/computer-standards-and-interfaces) | Weak–Moderate: focuses on standards, interfaces, and software quality; security yes, but mainly in standards context. | Verify indexing. | Could be framed as **calibration policy for FL‑IDS**, but lacks direct standardization angle. | Would need stronger emphasis on guidelines/standards and perhaps integration into reference architectures. | High – significant scope mismatch likely. | Low priority. |
| 8 | Ad Hoc Networks  [sciencedirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/journal/ad-hoc-networks) | Weak: focuses on ad hoc and sensor networks; security is included but network protocols and architectures dominate. | Verify indexing. | Would require reframing DATP for sensor/ad hoc networks rather than IoT botnets specifically. | Major narrative rework and possibly extra network‑layer experiments. | High – risk of “not in scope”. | Not recommended. |

***

# 13. Three-Level Expansion Roadmap

## 13.1 Minimal Journal Extension

(Aim: smallest credible extension that could pass in a mid‑tier venue; **not recommended as final choice**.)

| Component | Required Action | Why It Is Needed | Effort | Risk |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Dataset | Improve CICIoT2023 partition (device/host/time‑aware) and rerun B1–B2–B4. | Provides a second meaningful IoT scenario without adding a new dataset. |---|---|---|---|---|

| Baselines | Implement summary‑statistics global threshold; optionally one personalization baseline (FedBN or Per‑FedAvg) on N‑BaIoT only. ## 13.3 Ambitious Journal Extension

(Aim: maximal strength; high workload; **not recommended as primary goal**.)

| Component | Required Action | Why It Is Needed | Effort | Risk |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Datasets | Add two new IoT/IIoT datasets (e.g., Edge‑IIoTset and ToN‑IoT) plus improved CICIoT2023 partition. | Shows DATP across three heterogeneous IoT datasets; strongest generalization story. | Very High | Large engineering workload; risk of inconsistent client definitions and scope drift. |
| Baselines | Add summary‑stats global threshold, FedBN, Per‑FedAvg, and one learned threshold model (MLP‑based). | Comprehensive comparison against threshold and model‑personalization SOTA.  [arxiv](https://arxiv.org/html/2410.09284v1) | Very High | Paper may become a benchmarking zoo; DATP’s identity diluted. |
| Threshold variants | Implement many variants (local heuristics, conformal thresholding, etc.). | Exhaustive threshold survey. | Very High | Strong scope drift; may become threshold‑methods paper rather than DATP. |
| Temporal | Multi‑dataset temporal drift analysis with several recalibration strategies. | Strong but heavy; closer to longitudinal deployment study. | High | Data limitations and analysis complexity; risk of inconclusive results. |
| Deeper analyses | Almost all listed analyses plus privacy leakage experiments and light poisoning scenarios. | Comprehensive understanding, including robustness. | High | Risk of over‑claiming; limited space in journal article. |

***

# 14. Final Recommended Package

**Recommended level:** **Strong journal extension** (Section 13.2), constrained as requested.

1. **Dataset additions (max 2; use 1 in must‑do):**  
   - **Must‑do:** Add **one** new IoT/IIoT dataset with a clear device/host client notion (prefer Edge‑IIoTset or ToN‑IoT, selected after a quick feasibility check). [frontiersin](https://www.frontiersin.org/journals/big-data/articles/10.3389/fdata.2025.1526480/full)
   - **Optional:** Improved CICIoT2023 partition (counts as new regime, not new dataset).

2. **Baseline additions (max 3 families):**  
   - **Must‑do #1:** Summary‑statistics global threshold baseline (Laridi‑style). [arxiv](https://arxiv.org/html/2410.09284v1)
   - **Must‑do #2:** One simple local heuristic threshold (e.g., Local‑MinMax or Local‑IQR) to show p95 is not a cherry‑picked heuristic. [arxiv](https://arxiv.org/html/2410.09284v1)
   - **Should‑do #3 (if resources):** One personalization baseline (FedBN or Per‑FedAvg) on N‑BaIoT only. [sciencedirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S1110016825009810)

3. **Threshold additions (max 4 variants):**  
   - Quantile sweep (B1/B2/B4 at q=0.90, 0.95, 0.99). [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/54884680/7ec30c4e-be1a-4fa0-b512-ec2a89e1b24a/DATP-2.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEYNG77JJY&Signature=SKSXxKjHlouVeY4i09ca4sRbLGk%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEGsaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJHMEUCIQDFD8U6n20wgYy1lIWIUpx72WUp1%2BGzNhldJ8KR7WlnWAIgVSnYqCDWyvA0z%2B%2BMGA7xMDyMknLgcrZJGBYD8Z07NFgq8wQINBABGgw2OTk3NTMzMDk3MDUiDIgD5Me8%2FBcD9UTOoCrQBB9K5xQ66rGx9FVJ367oGZzxh%2ByEF3N5yU4FUrqbWcLkeilDY3MKsEdF5p7fNvuEpQ0Eyxf%2BWvBF6VifAtqi%2B8HcY%2Fwof0Pzg8sCvoHwwBpJj3ftj2h2wLqSu79JWq%2BnC1e4u0sZm2OaBiFeufhflrrAqTWMVuVcx4cuohoW4LLY5S1YhWmgywpZXNKmujmhbAaEDIHVSRhp94gtFkLUHwi5bDdSnBejGKJKBe7M%2BK9xueEfWTpGaLA9aFAioS2rvc%2BJb0g5ZFwW2lkOvJ7A88lCGT7%2BpaRz2NU7MlAu6BYezDgEjd%2F34CwqwJTCJFWOg1xTXHp2ByTWLYTWWBCf9ckOcLB2NtQz6Y3xSL3pEQ9IxMMskGNUpDQgIT8Cu4%2BTTTtcZ6CjqLdLMi5SDklTnAeYx2ueJpGOLy2RSXvSqg%2Fp0dE%2BuDJrnGcYGNy%2B42Ur6n%2BcPoWkNo2ZfYrTaMTesRPqxqBklXDqh1MJNLRGwFRtm6TzA3N6WSU97oKFIULgKVERss%2B7f%2BrIjbf6ns3vuOfopD4uGVi77CisoDINPNgvlJL3jPNHUvTpNpsGs%2F9mcGCErrI6ppw2zvEqRoE5pH8yn7wkiWDK5Uy83w58ze6hjYjBUDGQBf9M68SUCu%2BwYjzGRZf1U1W0CZOFR4mJCldbYj79NB2IsnvM%2BCg9%2B9u%2FahEs%2FXH67Q2lPtNgIYLqO6BP3w4XE9Qtn4MUd2Zr0Ke2udWY2R5BfSDLWxqwW9n3UbQ4hXcSCGi68cYLp53ByhArGWvkVcI0GmqICP8ZjVYwp4vG0AY6mAHjy%2FNerQHKG%2F7RMQtjydR%2Bq6jb3N9S44wIeSfIs7VhVQ3nHYzSJJkoAuGHCSRe4wjRREgZV5JEQYr94XlTMcit6HLxOBRGWPn9TxzfHGy6uwsoQ1sUF5ud6i2bY%2B3M2xwY0xNcVvpwwCgiRxQpgJuFYfB3umIN3%2Fd3lsocKZdTQgND0mlvHvCAocBswrSMUvnkl2V042gobQ%3D%3D&Expires=1779536244)
   - Local‑global shrinkage τk(λ).  
   - Calibration‑size‑aware fallback (tied to shrinkage).  
   - Summary‑statistics global threshold.

4. **Temporal/recalibration additions (max 1 family):**  
   - Single **N‑BaIoT temporal experiment family**: static vs periodic recalibration across time windows for B1, B2, B4, and shrinkage variants.

5. **Deeper analyses (max 6):**  
   - Client‑level benign/attack reconstruction‑error distributions.  
   - Heterogeneity vs benefit correlation (JS/Wasserstein vs ∆).  
   - Calibration‑size sensitivity (nmin and subsampling).  
   - Bootstrap CIs for key metrics.  
   - Operational false‑alarm burden per device.  
   - Threshold shift vs TPR loss for key devices.

6. **New figures:**  
   - Extended CV(FPR) vs α plots including summary‑stats threshold and new dataset.  
   - Temporal drift plots (CV(FPR), P10 Macro‑F1 over time).  
   - Reconstruction‑error distributions for representative devices.  
   - Scatter plots of divergence vs DATP benefit.

7. **New tables:**  
   - Expanded results tables for N‑BaIoT, new dataset, and improved CICIoT2023 partition including new baselines and CIs.  
   - Calibration‑size sensitivity table.  
   - Operational burden table (false alarms per device).  
   - Communication/metadata overhead table.

8. **New sections:**  
   - “Threshold Variants and Federated Threshold Baselines” (including summary‑stats baseline).  
   - “Temporal Drift and Recalibration”.  
   - “Fairness and Operational Burden”.  
   - “Post‑2022 FL IoT IDS and Federated Thresholding”.

9. **Supplementary material:**  
   - Full per‑client/seed results, additional threshold variants, full ablation of shrinkage and nmin, any optional personalization or adversarial experiments.

10. **Claims to strengthen:**  
    - DATP as a **device‑aware threshold personalization framework** that:  
      - Substantially reduces FPR dispersion under non‑IID heterogeneity,  
      - Offers a taxonomy‑free approximation via clustering,  
      - Behaves predictably under heterogeneity severity and temporal drift, and  
      - Remains relevant even when sophisticated global thresholding schemes are available. [arxiv](https://arxiv.org/html/2410.09284v1)

11. **Claims to avoid:**  
    - Any implication that DATP improves robustness to poisoning/evasion (unless you add proper experiments),  
    - Any strong privacy claim (e.g., “privacy‑preserving thresholds”) without formal mechanisms,  
    - Any implication that DATP replaces model personalization or robust aggregation rather than complementing them. [sciencedirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S1110016825009810)

***

[arxiv](https://arxiv.org/html/2410.09284v1) | New threshold computations. | “In our experiments, a federated summary‑statistics global threshold reduces FPR dispersion compared to simple shared thresholds but remains less effective than device‑aware calibration in the most heterogeneous regimes.” |
| DATP thresholds remain stable over realistic temporal drifts with modest recalibration. | Requires new experiments. | Temporal windows and recalibration analysis. | New time‑split evaluation artifacts. | “On N‑BaIoT, per‑client thresholds calibrated on early benign data maintain acceptable CV(FPR) and detection quality over [time window], and periodic recalibration further stabilizes these metrics under the tested drift conditions.” |
| B4 cluster‑mean calibration is a privacy‑preserving alternative to B2. | Should **not** be claimed. | Would need formal privacy analysis and attacks. | N/A | “B4 reduces dispersion using cluster‑mean thresholds derived from benign reconstruction‑error summaries but leaks distributional metadata; we therefore treat it as a calibration mechanism, not a privacy mechanism.”  [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/54884680/7ec30c4e-be1a-4fa0-b512-ec2a89e1b24a/DATP-2.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEYNG77JJY&Signature=SKSXxKjHlouVeY4i09ca4sRbLGk%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEGsaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJHMEUCIQDFD8U6n20wgYy1lIWIUpx72WUp1%2BGzNhldJ8KR7WlnWAIgVSnYqCDWyvA0z%2B%2BMGA7xMDyMknLgcrZJGBYD8Z07NFgq8wQINBABGgw2OTk3NTMzMDk3MDUiDIgD5Me8%2FBcD9UTOoCrQBB9K5xQ66rGx9FVJ367oGZzxh%2ByEF3N5yU4FUrqbWcLkeilDY3MKsEdF5p7fNvuEpQ0Eyxf%2BWvBF6VifAtqi%2B8HcY%2Fwof0Pzg8sCvoHwwBpJj3ftj2h2wLqSu79JWq%2BnC1e4u0sZm2OaBiFeufhflrrAqTWMVuVcx4cuohoW4LLY5S1YhWmgywpZXNKmujmhbAaEDIHVSRhp94gtFkLUHwi5bDdSnBejGKJKBe7M%2BK9xueEfWTpGaLA9aFAioS2rvc%2BJb0g5ZFwW2lkOvJ7A88lCGT7%2BpaRz2NU7MlAu6BYezDgEjd%2F34CwqwJTCJFWOg1xTXHp2ByTWLYTWWBCf9ckOcLB2NtQz6Y3xSL3pEQ9IxMMskGNUpDQgIT8Cu4%2BTTTtcZ6CjqLdLMi5SDklTnAeYx2ueJpGOLy2RSXvSqg%2Fp0dE%2BuDJrnGcYGNy%2B42Ur6n%2BcPoWkNo2ZfYrTaMTesRPqxqBklXDqh1MJNLRGwFRtm6TzA3N6WSU97oKFIULgKVERss%2B7f%2BrIjbf6ns3vuOfopD4uGVi77CisoDINPNgvlJL3jPNHUvTpNpsGs%2F9mcGCErrI6ppw2zvEqRoE5pH8yn7wkiWDK5Uy83w58ze6hjYjBUDGQBf9M68SUCu%2BwYjzGRZf1U1W0CZOFR4mJCldbYj79NB2IsnvM%2BCg9%2B9u%2FahEs%2FXH67Q2lPtNgIYLqO6BP3w4XE9Qtn4MUd2Zr0Ke2udWY2R5BfSDLWxqwW9n3UbQ4hXcSCGi68cYLp53ByhArGWvkVcI0GmqICP8ZjVYwp4vG0AY6mAHjy%2FNerQHKG%2F7RMQtjydR%2Bq6jb3N9S44wIeSfIs7VhVQ3nHYzSJJkoAuGHCSRe4wjRREgZV5JEQYr94XlTMcit6HLxOBRGWPn9TxzfHGy6uwsoQ1sUF5ud6i2bY%2B3M2xwY0xNcVvpwwCgiRxQpgJuFYfB3umIN3%2Fd3lsocKZdTQgND0mlvHvCAocBswrSMUvnkl2V042gobQ%3D%3D&Expires=1779536244) |
| DATP improves robustness to poisoning/evasion. | Should not be claimed without new experiments. | Poisoning/evasion experiments. | N/A (unless added). | “Our evaluation is limited to clean Mirai/BASHLITE traffic; robustness to poisoning or evasion attacks remains future work.”  [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/54884680/7ec30c4e-be1a-4fa0-b512-ec2a89e1b24a/DATP-2.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEYNG77JJY&Signature=SKSXxKjHlouVeY4i09ca4sRbLGk%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEGsaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJHMEUCIQDFD8U6n20wgYy1lIWIUpx72WUp1%2BGzNhldJ8KR7WlnWAIgVSnYqCDWyvA0z%2B%2BMGA7xMDyMknLgcrZJGBYD8Z07NFgq8wQINBABGgw2OTk3NTMzMDk3MDUiDIgD5Me8%2FBcD9UTOoCrQBB9K5xQ66rGx9FVJ367oGZzxh%2ByEF3N5yU4FUrqbWcLkeilDY3MKsEdF5p7fNvuEpQ0Eyxf%2BWvBF6VifAtqi%2B8HcY%2Fwof0Pzg8sCvoHwwBpJj3ftj2h2wLqSu79JWq%2BnC1e4u0sZm2OaBiFeufhflrrAqTWMVuVcx4cuohoW4LLY5S1YhWmgywpZXNKmujmhbAaEDIHVSRhp94gtFkLUHwi5bDdSnBejGKJKBe7M%2BK9xueEfWTpGaLA9aFAioS2rvc%2BJb0g5ZFwW2lkOvJ7A88lCGT7%2BpaRz2NU7MlAu6BYezDgEjd%2F34CwqwJTCJFWOg1xTXHp2ByTWLYTWWBCf9ckOcLB2NtQz6Y3xSL3pEQ9IxMMskGNUpDQgIT8Cu4%2BTTTtcZ6CjqLdLMi5SDklTnAeYx2ueJpGOLy2RSXvSqg%2Fp0dE%2BuDJrnGcYGNy%2B42Ur6n%2BcPoWkNo2ZfYrTaMTesRPqxqBklXDqh1MJNLRGwFRtm6TzA3N6WSU97oKFIULgKVERss%2B7f%2BrIjbf6ns3vuOfopD4uGVi77CisoDINPNgvlJL3jPNHUvTpNpsGs%2F9mcGCErrI6ppw2zvEqRoE5pH8yn7wkiWDK5Uy83w58ze6hjYjBUDGQBf9M68SUCu%2BwYjzGRZf1U1W0CZOFR4mJCldbYj79NB2IsnvM%2BCg9%2B9u%2FahEs%2FXH67Q2lPtNgIYLqO6BP3w4XE9Qtn4MUd2Zr0Ke2udWY2R5BfSDLWxqwW9n3UbQ4hXcSCGi68cYLp53ByhArGWvkVcI0GmqICP8ZjVYwp4vG0AY6mAHjy%2FNerQHKG%2F7RMQtjydR%2Bq6jb3N9S44wIeSfIs7VhVQ3nHYzSJJkoAuGHCSRe4wjRREgZV5JEQYr94XlTMcit6HLxOBRGWPn9TxzfHGy6uwsoQ1sUF5ud6i2bY%2B3M2xwY0xNcVvpwwCgiRxQpgJuFYfB3umIN3%2Fd3lsocKZdTQgND0mlvHvCAocBswrSMUvnkl2V042gobQ%3D%3D&Expires=1779536244) |
| DATP is still needed when model personalization is deployed. | Requires new experiments (FedBN/Per‑FedAvg baseline). | One personalization baseline on N‑BaIoT.  [sciencedirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S1110016825009810) | New training runs. | “Preliminary experiments with [FedBN/Per‑FedAvg] suggest that even when local model components are personalized, per‑client thresholds can still reduce FPR dispersion further under the tested N‑BaIoT configuration; a full exploration of personalization–threshold interactions is left for future work.” |

# 16. Reviewer-Loophole Closure Table

| Loophole | Closed By | Remaining Risk | Final Wording Discipline |
|---|---|---|---|
| “Single‑dataset” criticism | Add Edge‑IIoTset/ToN‑IoT + improved CICIoT2023 partition. | If new dataset is weakly partitioned, criticism persists. | Always phrase generalization claims as “on the tested datasets and partitions” and emphasize heterogeneity‑measured patterns. |
| “What about federated thresholding SOTA?” | Implement and compare with summary‑stats global threshold.  [arxiv](https://arxiv.org/html/2410.09284v1) | Approximation differences vs original method; must avoid over‑claiming. | Explicitly acknowledge method origin, describe your implementation as an adaptation, and limit claims to “under our implementation and datasets”. |
| “Drift and recalibration ignored” | Add temporal drift and recalibration experiment on N‑BaIoT. | If drift is weak in N‑BaIoT, results may be inconclusive. | Frame temporal results as “under the observed drift in N‑BaIoT” and avoid universal statements; highlight as initial exploration. |
| “Privacy analysis missing” | Dedicated subsection comparing DATP fingerprints with summary‑statistics privacy claims; qualitative analysis.  [arxiv](https://arxiv.org/html/2410.09284v1) | No formal DP or leakage bounds; some reviewers may want more. | Use cautious language: “may leak”, “should be protected by”, “we do not quantify”; avoid “privacy‑preserving”. |
| “No comparison to personalization methods” | Optional FedBN/Per‑FedAvg baseline on N‑BaIoT.  [sciencedirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S1110016825009810) | If omitted, reviewer can still criticize; but pointing to SoA and scope helps. | If baseline omitted due to time, explicitly state in limitations: “we focus on threshold scope holding the encoder fixed; model personalization is complementary future work.” |
| “Temporal scale and overhead unrealistic” | Overhead table and drift experiment with realistic calibration/sample budgets. | Overhead estimates approximate, not measured on hardware. | Clarify that overhead is approximated from message sizes and that hardware‑level profiling is future work. |
| “Conference extension not substantial” | New datasets, baselines, temporal experiments, and analyses plus explicit extension statement.  [astesj](https://astesj.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/10/conference-paper-extension.pdf) | If overlap in figures/text remains high, some editors may still worry. | Ensure first citation is to conference version; explicitly list new contributions; avoid reusing identical figures/tables and large text blocks. |

***

# 17. Final Recommended Decision Gate

## 17.1 Best Target Journal  

**Computers & Security** is the best Elsevier target: it has a strong track record in FL‑IDS, IoT security, and anomaly detection, and it explicitly targets security professionals and researchers dealing with privacy and robustness. [sciencedirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/abs/pii/S1389128623004504)

## 17.2 Best Expansion Level  

Choose **Strong** (Section 13.2): it balances feasibility with the level of novelty and breadth usually expected in C&S or JNCA.

## 17.3 Exact Must-Do List Before Submission  

1. **Add one new IoT/IIoT dataset** with a meaningful client notion (Edge‑IIoTset or ToN‑IoT), run full B1–B2–B4 + summary‑stats threshold analysis. [frontiersin](https://www.frontiersin.org/journals/big-data/articles/10.3389/fdata.2025.1526480/full)
2. **Redesign CICIoT2023 partition** into device/host/time‑aware clients and rerun B1–B2–B4 (and summary‑stats baseline). [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/collection_2068727c-5b13-4337-9ec8-46f9c623d7fe/275fd68a-efa9-445b-954b-e817bc2c64c9/State_of_the_Art.md)
3. **Implement summary‑statistics global threshold** baseline à la Laridi et al. on all datasets and compare against B1/B2/B4. [arxiv](https://arxiv.org/html/2410.09284v1)
4. **Add quantile sweep and local‑global shrinkage threshold variants** (with calibration‑size awareness) and report their impact on CV(FPR), P10 Macro‑F1, and mean FPR.  
5. **Run a temporal drift/recalibration experiment** on N‑BaIoT (static vs periodic recalibration). [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/54884680/7ec30c4e-be1a-4fa0-b512-ec2a89e1b24a/DATP-2.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEYNG77JJY&Signature=SKSXxKjHlouVeY4i09ca4sRbLGk%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEGsaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJHMEUCIQDFD8U6n20wgYy1lIWIUpx72WUp1%2BGzNhldJ8KR7WlnWAIgVSnYqCDWyvA0z%2B%2BMGA7xMDyMknLgcrZJGBYD8Z07NFgq8wQINBABGgw2OTk3NTMzMDk3MDUiDIgD5Me8%2FBcD9UTOoCrQBB9K5xQ66rGx9FVJ367oGZzxh%2ByEF3N5yU4FUrqbWcLkeilDY3MKsEdF5p7fNvuEpQ0Eyxf%2BWvBF6VifAtqi%2B8HcY%2Fwof0Pzg8sCvoHwwBpJj3ftj2h2wLqSu79JWq%2BnC1e4u0sZm2OaBiFeufhflrrAqTWMVuVcx4cuohoW4LLY5S1YhWmgywpZXNKmujmhbAaEDIHVSRhp94gtFkLUHwi5bDdSnBejGKJKBe7M%2BK9xueEfWTpGaLA9aFAioS2rvc%2BJb0g5ZFwW2lkOvJ7A88lCGT7%2BpaRz2NU7MlAu6BYezDgEjd%2F34CwqwJTCJFWOg1xTXHp2ByTWLYTWWBCf9ckOcLB2NtQz6Y3xSL3pEQ9IxMMskGNUpDQgIT8Cu4%2BTTTtcZ6CjqLdLMi5SDklTnAeYx2ueJpGOLy2RSXvSqg%2Fp0dE%2BuDJrnGcYGNy%2B42Ur6n%2BcPoWkNo2ZfYrTaMTesRPqxqBklXDqh1MJNLRGwFRtm6TzA3N6WSU97oKFIULgKVERss%2B7f%2BrIjbf6ns3vuOfopD4uGVi77CisoDINPNgvlJL3jPNHUvTpNpsGs%2F9mcGCErrI6ppw2zvEqRoE5pH8yn7wkiWDK5Uy83w58ze6hjYjBUDGQBf9M68SUCu%2BwYjzGRZf1U1W0CZOFR4mJCldbYj79NB2IsnvM%2BCg9%2B9u%2FahEs%2FXH67Q2lPtNgIYLqO6BP3w4XE9Qtn4MUd2Zr0Ke2udWY2R5BfSDLWxqwW9n3UbQ4hXcSCGi68cYLp53ByhArGWvkVcI0GmqICP8ZjVYwp4vG0AY6mAHjy%2FNerQHKG%2F7RMQtjydR%2Bq6jb3N9S44wIeSfIs7VhVQ3nHYzSJJkoAuGHCSRe4wjRREgZV5JEQYr94XlTMcit6HLxOBRGWPn9TxzfHGy6uwsoQ1sUF5ud6i2bY%2B3M2xwY0xNcVvpwwCgiRxQpgJuFYfB3umIN3%2Fd3lsocKZdTQgND0mlvHvCAocBswrSMUvnkl2V042gobQ%3D%3D&Expires=1779536244)
6. **Perform deeper analyses:** reconstruction‑error distributions, heterogeneity vs DATP benefit, calibration‑size sensitivity, operational false‑alarm burden, and bootstrap CIs for key metrics. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/54884680/d7bca94c-149b-43b0-923a-7f635d7ab3f7/State_of_the_Art.md?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEYNG77JJY&Signature=%2BZWkfVFuHRTcIbiief1CY6bsKa0%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEGsaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJHMEUCIQDFD8U6n20wgYy1lIWIUpx72WUp1%2BGzNhldJ8KR7WlnWAIgVSnYqCDWyvA0z%2B%2BMGA7xMDyMknLgcrZJGBYD8Z07NFgq8wQINBABGgw2OTk3NTMzMDk3MDUiDIgD5Me8%2FBcD9UTOoCrQBB9K5xQ66rGx9FVJ367oGZzxh%2ByEF3N5yU4FUrqbWcLkeilDY3MKsEdF5p7fNvuEpQ0Eyxf%2BWvBF6VifAtqi%2B8HcY%2Fwof0Pzg8sCvoHwwBpJj3ftj2h2wLqSu79JWq%2BnC1e4u0sZm2OaBiFeufhflrrAqTWMVuVcx4cuohoW4LLY5S1YhWmgywpZXNKmujmhbAaEDIHVSRhp94gtFkLUHwi5bDdSnBejGKJKBe7M%2BK9xueEfWTpGaLA9aFAioS2rvc%2BJb0g5ZFwW2lkOvJ7A88lCGT7%2BpaRz2NU7MlAu6BYezDgEjd%2F34CwqwJTCJFWOg1xTXHp2ByTWLYTWWBCf9ckOcLB2NtQz6Y3xSL3pEQ9IxMMskGNUpDQgIT8Cu4%2BTTTtcZ6CjqLdLMi5SDklTnAeYx2ueJpGOLy2RSXvSqg%2Fp0dE%2BuDJrnGcYGNy%2B42Ur6n%2BcPoWkNo2ZfYrTaMTesRPqxqBklXDqh1MJNLRGwFRtm6TzA3N6WSU97oKFIULgKVERss%2B7f%2BrIjbf6ns3vuOfopD4uGVi77CisoDINPNgvlJL3jPNHUvTpNpsGs%2F9mcGCErrI6ppw2zvEqRoE5pH8yn7wkiWDK5Uy83w58ze6hjYjBUDGQBf9M68SUCu%2BwYjzGRZf1U1W0CZOFR4mJCldbYj79NB2IsnvM%2BCg9%2B9u%2FahEs%2FXH67Q2lPtNgIYLqO6BP3w4XE9Qtn4MUd2Zr0Ke2udWY2R5BfSDLWxqwW9n3UbQ4hXcSCGi68cYLp53ByhArGWvkVcI0GmqICP8ZjVYwp4vG0AY6mAHjy%2FNerQHKG%2F7RMQtjydR%2Bq6jb3N9S44wIeSfIs7VhVQ3nHYzSJJkoAuGHCSRe4wjRREgZV5JEQYr94XlTMcit6HLxOBRGWPn9TxzfHGy6uwsoQ1sUF5ud6i2bY%2B3M2xwY0xNcVvpwwCgiRxQpgJuFYfB3umIN3%2Fd3lsocKZdTQgND0mlvHvCAocBswrSMUvnkl2V042gobQ%3D%3D&Expires=1779536244)
7. **Update related work** to include 2022–2025 FL‑IDS and federated thresholding papers (FedMSE, Tab‑Transformer FL IDS, SciRep FL IDS, edge–cloud AE+MLP thresholding, summary‑stats thresholding), and clearly position DATP relative to them. [salzburgresearch](https://www.salzburgresearch.at/publikation/federated-learning-for-anomaly-detection-in-edge-cloud-communication-systems/)
8. **Prepare a clear extension statement and cover letter**, citing the conference paper and enumerating new contributions; ensure figures and tables are substantially updated. [astesj](https://astesj.com/wp-content/uploads/2016/10/conference-paper-extension.pdf)

## 17.4 Exact Do-Not-Do List  

1. Do **not** add more than **one new dataset** in the main paper (a second new dataset can be left as future work) to avoid over‑stretching.  
2. Do **not** introduce many baseline families (limit to summary‑stats global threshold, one local heuristic, and at most one personalization baseline).  
3. Do **not** attempt a full poisoning/backdoor/evasion study unless you can dedicate significant time; keep adversarial analysis, if any, small and clearly scoped. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/54884680/d7bca94c-149b-43b0-923a-7f635d7ab3f7/State_of_the_Art.md?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEYNG77JJY&Signature=%2BZWkfVFuHRTcIbiief1CY6bsKa0%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEGsaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJHMEUCIQDFD8U6n20wgYy1lIWIUpx72WUp1%2BGzNhldJ8KR7WlnWAIgVSnYqCDWyvA0z%2B%2BMGA7xMDyMknLgcrZJGBYD8Z07NFgq8wQINBABGgw2OTk3NTMzMDk3MDUiDIgD5Me8%2FBcD9UTOoCrQBB9K5xQ66rGx9FVJ367oGZzxh%2ByEF3N5yU4FUrqbWcLkeilDY3MKsEdF5p7fNvuEpQ0Eyxf%2BWvBF6VifAtqi%2B8HcY%2Fwof0Pzg8sCvoHwwBpJj3ftj2h2wLqSu79JWq%2BnC1e4u0sZm2OaBiFeufhflrrAqTWMVuVcx4cuohoW4LLY5S1YhWmgywpZXNKmujmhbAaEDIHVSRhp94gtFkLUHwi5bDdSnBejGKJKBe7M%2BK9xueEfWTpGaLA9aFAioS2rvc%2BJb0g5ZFwW2lkOvJ7A88lCGT7%2BpaRz2NU7MlAu6BYezDgEjd%2F34CwqwJTCJFWOg1xTXHp2ByTWLYTWWBCf9ckOcLB2NtQz6Y3xSL3pEQ9IxMMskGNUpDQgIT8Cu4%2BTTTtcZ6CjqLdLMi5SDklTnAeYx2ueJpGOLy2RSXvSqg%2Fp0dE%2BuDJrnGcYGNy%2B42Ur6n%2BcPoWkNo2ZfYrTaMTesRPqxqBklXDqh1MJNLRGwFRtm6TzA3N6WSU97oKFIULgKVERss%2B7f%2BrIjbf6ns3vuOfopD4uGVi77CisoDINPNgvlJL3jPNHUvTpNpsGs%2F9mcGCErrI6ppw2zvEqRoE5pH8yn7wkiWDK5Uy83w58ze6hjYjBUDGQBf9M68SUCu%2BwYjzGRZf1U1W0CZOFR4mJCldbYj79NB2IsnvM%2BCg9%2B9u%2FahEs%2FXH67Q2lPtNgIYLqO6BP3w4XE9Qtn4MUd2Zr0Ke2udWY2R5BfSDLWxqwW9n3UbQ4hXcSCGi68cYLp53ByhArGWvkVcI0GmqICP8ZjVYwp4vG0AY6mAHjy%2FNerQHKG%2F7RMQtjydR%2Bq6jb3N9S44wIeSfIs7VhVQ3nHYzSJJkoAuGHCSRe4wjRREgZV5JEQYr94XlTMcit6HLxOBRGWPn9TxzfHGy6uwsoQ1sUF5ud6i2bY%2B3M2xwY0xNcVvpwwCgiRxQpgJuFYfB3umIN3%2Fd3lsocKZdTQgND0mlvHvCAocBswrSMUvnkl2V042gobQ%3D%3D&Expires=1779536244)
4. Do **not** turn DATP into a general FL‑IDS algorithm comparison paper; keep FedAvg AE as the primary model and treat other methods as context or limited baselines.  
5. Do **not** claim formal privacy or robustness guarantees; describe DATP as a calibration method that can be combined with privacy/robustness mechanisms. [arxiv](https://arxiv.org/html/2410.09284v1)
6. Do **not** rely on UNSW‑NB15, Bot‑IoT, or other non‑IoT‑specific datasets as primary evaluation datasets; if used at all, keep them clearly labelled as adjacent evidence. [frontiersin](https://www.frontiersin.org/journals/big-data/articles/10.3389/fdata.2025.1526480/full)

## 17.5 Should the Journal Extension Wait Until Conference Acceptance?  

No, you do **not** need to wait for conference acceptance to prepare the journal extension, but you should wait to **submit** to C&S (or another Elsevier journal) until the conference decision is known, so you can:  

- Include the final reference to the conference version (or note that it is under review if still pending),  
- Ensure there is no conflict with conference copyright, and  
- Tailor the extension narrative to the conference reviews once available. [elsevier](https://www.elsevier.com/publishing/publish-in-a-journal)

***

# 19. Final Red-Team Verdict

## 19.1 Would This Survive a Strong Elsevier Review?  

If you implement the **Strong** package as specified—one new IoT/IIoT dataset, improved CICIoT2023 partition, summary‑stats global threshold baseline, temporal drift analysis, constrained threshold variants, and deeper analyses with updated related work—the resulting paper should be robust against most standard reviewer attacks for Computers & Security, Computer Networks, or JNCA. The key is to keep DATP’s focus tight (device‑aware threshold personalization) while demonstrating cross‑dataset generality and engaging directly with 2024–2025 federated thresholding and FL‑IDS work. [sciencedirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S1110016825009810)

## 19.2 What Would Still Be Attacked?  

Unavoidable residual attack surfaces:

- Fleet size may still be modest (e.g., 9 devices in N‑BaIoT plus tens of clients in Edge‑IIoTset/CICIoT2023), leaving questions about behavior at hundreds of clients. [frontiersin](https://www.frontiersin.org/journals/big-data/articles/10.3389/fdata.2025.1526480/full)
- Temporal drift experiments may be limited by available timestamps and drift magnitude; some reviewers may want more realistic longitudinal deployments. [salzburgresearch](https://www.salzburgresearch.at/publikation/federated-learning-for-anomaly-detection-in-edge-cloud-communication-systems/)
- Privacy analysis of B4 fingerprints will remain qualitative unless you invest in formal leakage quantification or DP; some privacy specialists may ask for more. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/collection_2068727c-5b13-4337-9ec8-46f9c623d7fe/27d48e5f-d728-46d6-940e-7d5f894f218f/Gap-Limitation-Ledger.md)
- Model personalization and robust aggregation will still be treated somewhat peripherally; reviewers deeply invested in FedBN, FedMSE, or poisoning defenses may prefer more extensive comparisons. [sciencedirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S1110016825009810)

These are acceptable if you **explicitly acknowledge** them in the limitations section and keep claims modest.

## 19.3 Final Priority Order (Top 10 Actions)

1. **Add one new IoT/IIoT dataset** with a clear client notion and run full B1–B2–B4 (+ summary‑stats global threshold) analysis.  
2. **Redesign CICIoT2023 partition** into meaningful clients and rerun DATP’s threshold policies plus summary‑stats baseline.  
3. **Implement summary‑statistics global threshold** on all datasets and compare to B1/B2/B4, especially under non‑IID severity sweeps. [arxiv](https://arxiv.org/html/2410.09284v1)
4. **Design and run N‑BaIoT temporal drift/recalibration experiments**, including static vs periodic recalibration. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/54884680/7ec30c4e-be1a-4fa0-b512-ec2a89e1b24a/DATP-2.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEYNG77JJY&Signature=SKSXxKjHlouVeY4i09ca4sRbLGk%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEGsaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJHMEUCIQDFD8U6n20wgYy1lIWIUpx72WUp1%2BGzNhldJ8KR7WlnWAIgVSnYqCDWyvA0z%2B%2BMGA7xMDyMknLgcrZJGBYD8Z07NFgq8wQINBABGgw2OTk3NTMzMDk3MDUiDIgD5Me8%2FBcD9UTOoCrQBB9K5xQ66rGx9FVJ367oGZzxh%2ByEF3N5yU4FUrqbWcLkeilDY3MKsEdF5p7fNvuEpQ0Eyxf%2BWvBF6VifAtqi%2B8HcY%2Fwof0Pzg8sCvoHwwBpJj3ftj2h2wLqSu79JWq%2BnC1e4u0sZm2OaBiFeufhflrrAqTWMVuVcx4cuohoW4LLY5S1YhWmgywpZXNKmujmhbAaEDIHVSRhp94gtFkLUHwi5bDdSnBejGKJKBe7M%2BK9xueEfWTpGaLA9aFAioS2rvc%2BJb0g5ZFwW2lkOvJ7A88lCGT7%2BpaRz2NU7MlAu6BYezDgEjd%2F34CwqwJTCJFWOg1xTXHp2ByTWLYTWWBCf9ckOcLB2NtQz6Y3xSL3pEQ9IxMMskGNUpDQgIT8Cu4%2BTTTtcZ6CjqLdLMi5SDklTnAeYx2ueJpGOLy2RSXvSqg%2Fp0dE%2BuDJrnGcYGNy%2B42Ur6n%2BcPoWkNo2ZfYrTaMTesRPqxqBklXDqh1MJNLRGwFRtm6TzA3N6WSU97oKFIULgKVERss%2B7f%2BrIjbf6ns3vuOfopD4uGVi77CisoDINPNgvlJL3jPNHUvTpNpsGs%2F9mcGCErrI6ppw2zvEqRoE5pH8yn7wkiWDK5Uy83w58ze6hjYjBUDGQBf9M68SUCu%2BwYjzGRZf1U1W0CZOFR4mJCldbYj79NB2IsnvM%2BCg9%2B9u%2FahEs%2FXH67Q2lPtNgIYLqO6BP3w4XE9Qtn4MUd2Zr0Ke2udWY2R5BfSDLWxqwW9n3UbQ4hXcSCGi68cYLp53ByhArGWvkVcI0GmqICP8ZjVYwp4vG0AY6mAHjy%2FNerQHKG%2F7RMQtjydR%2Bq6jb3N9S44wIeSfIs7VhVQ3nHYzSJJkoAuGHCSRe4wjRREgZV5JEQYr94XlTMcit6HLxOBRGWPn9TxzfHGy6uwsoQ1sUF5ud6i2bY%2B3M2xwY0xNcVvpwwCgiRxQpgJuFYfB3umIN3%2Fd3lsocKZdTQgND0mlvHvCAocBswrSMUvnkl2V042gobQ%3D%3D&Expires=1779536244)
5. **Add quantile sweep and local‑global shrinkage threshold variants** (with calibration‑size awareness) and integrate them into the main results.  
6. **Perform deeper analyses**: heterogeneity vs benefit correlation, calibration‑size sensitivity, reconstruction‑error distributions, operational false‑alarm burden, and bootstrap CIs. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/54884680/d7bca94c-149b-43b0-923a-7f635d7ab3f7/State_of_the_Art.md?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEYNG77JJY&Signature=%2BZWkfVFuHRTcIbiief1CY6bsKa0%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEGsaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJHMEUCIQDFD8U6n20wgYy1lIWIUpx72WUp1%2BGzNhldJ8KR7WlnWAIgVSnYqCDWyvA0z%2B%2BMGA7xMDyMknLgcrZJGBYD8Z07NFgq8wQINBABGgw2OTk3NTMzMDk3MDUiDIgD5Me8%2FBcD9UTOoCrQBB9K5xQ66rGx9FVJ367oGZzxh%2ByEF3N5yU4FUrqbWcLkeilDY3MKsEdF5p7fNvuEpQ0Eyxf%2BWvBF6VifAtqi%2B8HcY%2Fwof0Pzg8sCvoHwwBpJj3ftj2h2wLqSu79JWq%2BnC1e4u0sZm2OaBiFeufhflrrAqTWMVuVcx4cuohoW4LLY5S1YhWmgywpZXNKmujmhbAaEDIHVSRhp94gtFkLUHwi5bDdSnBejGKJKBe7M%2BK9xueEfWTpGaLA9aFAioS2rvc%2BJb0g5ZFwW2lkOvJ7A88lCGT7%2BpaRz2NU7MlAu6BYezDgEjd%2F34CwqwJTCJFWOg1xTXHp2ByTWLYTWWBCf9ckOcLB2NtQz6Y3xSL3pEQ9IxMMskGNUpDQgIT8Cu4%2BTTTtcZ6CjqLdLMi5SDklTnAeYx2ueJpGOLy2RSXvSqg%2Fp0dE%2BuDJrnGcYGNy%2B42Ur6n%2BcPoWkNo2ZfYrTaMTesRPqxqBklXDqh1MJNLRGwFRtm6TzA3N6WSU97oKFIULgKVERss%2B7f%2BrIjbf6ns3vuOfopD4uGVi77CisoDINPNgvlJL3jPNHUvTpNpsGs%2F9mcGCErrI6ppw2zvEqRoE5pH8yn7wkiWDK5Uy83w58ze6hjYjBUDGQBf9M68SUCu%2BwYjzGRZf1U1W0CZOFR4mJCldbYj79NB2IsnvM%2BCg9%2B9u%2FahEs%2FXH67Q2lPtNgIYLqO6BP3w4XE9Qtn4MUd2Zr0Ke2udWY2R5BfSDLWxqwW9n3UbQ4hXcSCGi68cYLp53ByhArGWvkVcI0GmqICP8ZjVYwp4vG0AY6mAHjy%2FNerQHKG%2F7RMQtjydR%2Bq6jb3N9S44wIeSfIs7VhVQ3nHYzSJJkoAuGHCSRe4wjRREgZV5JEQYr94XlTMcit6HLxOBRGWPn9TxzfHGy6uwsoQ1sUF5ud6i2bY%2B3M2xwY0xNcVvpwwCgiRxQpgJuFYfB3umIN3%2Fd3lsocKZdTQgND0mlvHvCAocBswrSMUvnkl2V042gobQ%3D%3D&Expires=1779536244)
7. **Update related work** to cover 2022–2025 FL‑IDS and federated thresholding literature (FedMSE, Tab‑Transformer FL IDS, SciRep FL IDS, summary‑stats thresholding, edge–cloud AE+MLP). [nature](https://www.nature.com/articles/s41598-025-93501-8)
8. **Add a compact communication/metadata overhead estimate** and clarify that DATP overhead is negligible compared to model updates. [salzburgresearch](https://www.salzburgresearch.at/publikation/federated-learning-for-anomaly-detection-in-edge-cloud-communication-systems/)
9. **Optionally add one personalization baseline (FedBN or Per‑FedAvg)** on N‑BaIoT to clarify DATP’s niche relative to model personalization. [sciencedirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/pii/S1110016825009810)
10. **Prepare a clear conference‑extension narrative**, ensuring ≤40% overlap in figures/tables and substantially expanded experiments and analysis, and explicitly describing the extension in the cover letter and introduction. [sciencedirect](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/abs/pii/S0306261926006999)

If you execute this list, keep DATP’s focus on threshold personalization, and avoid over‑claiming on privacy and robustness, the journal extension should be both **feasible** and **defensible** in front of a demanding Elsevier editor.
